<h2>Timeline of German history</h2>

<tr>
<td>9</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Battle of the Teutoburg Forest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Teutoburg_Forest">Battle of the Teutoburg Forest</a>: An alliance of Germanic tribes ambushed and decisively destroyed three Roman legions and their auxiliaries, led by&nbsp;<a title="Publius Quinctilius Varus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Quinctilius_Varus">Publius Quinctilius Varus</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>15</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>

<tr>
<td>16</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Battle of the Angrivarian Wall" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Angrivarian_Wall">Battle of the Angrivarian Wall</a>&nbsp;fought near&nbsp;<a title="Porta Westfalica" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porta_Westfalica">Porta Westfalica</a>&nbsp;between the Roman general&nbsp;<a title="Germanicus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanicus">Germanicus</a>&nbsp;and an alliance of Germanic tribes commanded by&nbsp;<a title="Arminius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arminius">Arminius</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>16</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Battle of Idistaviso" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Idistaviso">Battle of Idistaviso</a>&nbsp;fought between Roman legions commanded by Roman emperor&nbsp;<a title="Tiberius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberius">Tiberius</a>' heir and adopted son Germanicus, and an alliance of Germanic peoples commanded by Arminius.</td>
</tr>

<td>500</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>

The law forbade women from inheriting land.</td>

<tr>
<td>28 November</td>

<td>30 April</td>
<td>The pro-<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine</a>&nbsp;<a title="Regent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regent">regent</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Ostrogothic Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom">Ostrogothic Kingdom</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Amalasuntha" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amalasuntha">Amalasuntha</a>, was murdered on the orders of her cousin and coregent&nbsp;<a title="Theodahad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodahad">Theodahad</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>

<tr>
<td>535</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Council of Clermont (535)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Clermont_(535)">Council of Clermont (535)</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;was held in modern&nbsp;<a title="Clermont-Ferrand" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clermont-Ferrand">Clermont-Ferrand</a>&nbsp;which limited the rights of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholicism">Catholic</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop (Catholic Church)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bishop_(Catholic_Church)">bishops</a>&nbsp;to appeal to the state and which condemned marriage between&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christians</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Jews</a>&nbsp;and between relatives.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">539</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Gothic War (535&ndash;554)</em>:&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;forces under&nbsp;<a title="Theudebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theudebert_I">Theudebert I</a>&nbsp;drove&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Ostrogothic Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom">Ostrogothic</a>&nbsp;armies from their encampments on the&nbsp;<a title="Po (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Po_(river)">Po</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>November</td>
<td><em>Gothic War (535&ndash;554)</em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;army on the&nbsp;<a title="Po (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Po_(river)">Po</a>, suffering from dysentery, surrendered to the&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantines</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>548</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Theudebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theudebert_I">Theudebert I</a>&nbsp;died. His son&nbsp;<a title="Theudebald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theudebald">Theudebald</a>&nbsp;inherited his kingdom.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>549</td>
<td>October</td>
<td><em><a title="Fifth Council of Orl&eacute;ans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Council_of_Orl%C3%A9ans">Fifth Council of Orl&eacute;ans</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;presided over by&nbsp;<a title="Sacerdos of Lyon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacerdos_of_Lyon">Sacerdos of Lyon</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Orl&eacute;ans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orl%C3%A9ans">Orl&eacute;ans</a>&nbsp;condemned&nbsp;<a title="Nestorianism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nestorianism">Nestorianism</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Simony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simony">simony</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>554</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Volturnus (554)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Volturnus_(554)">Battle of the Volturnus (554)</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine</a>&nbsp;force cut off and destroyed a joint&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>-<a title="Ostrogothic Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom">Ostrogothic</a>&nbsp;army at their camp on the&nbsp;<a title="Volturno" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volturno">Volturno</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Theudebald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theudebald">Theudebald</a>&nbsp;died, childless. His kingdom passed to&nbsp;<a title="Chlothar I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_I">Chlothar</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>558</td>
<td>13 December</td>
<td><a title="Childebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childebert_I">Childebert I</a>&nbsp;died without male heirs.&nbsp;<a title="Chlothar I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_I">Chlothar</a>&nbsp;inherited his kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>560</td>
<td>December</td>
<td><a title="Conomor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conomor">Conomor</a>,&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Domnon&eacute;e" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domnon%C3%A9e">Domnon&eacute;e</a>, who had allied with&nbsp;<a title="Chlothar I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_I">Chlothar's</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Chram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chram">Chram</a>&nbsp;against him, was killed in battle by Chlothar's forces.</td>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">561</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Chram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chram">Chram</a>&nbsp;was captured and executed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>29 November</td>
<td><a title="Chlothar I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_I">Chlothar</a>&nbsp;died of pneumonia. His kingdom was divided among his surviving sons&nbsp;<a title="Charibert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charibert_I">Charibert I</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Guntram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guntram">Guntram</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Sigebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigebert_I">Sigebert I</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Chilperic I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chilperic_I">Chilperic I</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>567</td>
<td>December</td>
<td><a title="Charibert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charibert_I">Charibert I</a>&nbsp;died. His kingdom was divided among his brothers&nbsp;<a title="Guntram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guntram">Guntram</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Chilperic I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chilperic_I">Chilperic I</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Sigebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigebert_I">Sigebert I</a>, the latter of whose domains become known as&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasia</a>, the eastern land, with its capital at&nbsp;<a title="Metz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metz">Metz</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td>575</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Sigebert I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigebert_I">Sigebert I</a>&nbsp;died. He was succeeded by his young son&nbsp;<a title="Childebert II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childebert_II">Childebert II</a>, with his wife&nbsp;<a title="Brunhilda of Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brunhilda_of_Austrasia">Brunhilda of Austrasia</a>&nbsp;acting as regent.</td>
</tr>

<td>September</td>
<td><a title="Chilperic I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chilperic_I">Chilperic I</a>&nbsp;was stabbed to death. His infant son&nbsp;<a title="Chlothar II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_II">Chlothar II the Great, the Young</a>&nbsp;inherited his kingdom under the regency of his mother&nbsp;<a title="Fredegund" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fredegund">Fredegund</a>.</td>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">612</td>

<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3" valign="top">613</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Theuderic II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theuderic_II">Theuderic II</a>&nbsp;died of dysentery. His young bastard son&nbsp;<a title="Sigebert II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigebert_II">Sigebert II</a>&nbsp;became&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasia</a>&nbsp;under the regency of&nbsp;<a title="Brunhilda of Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brunhilda_of_Austrasia">Brunhilda</a>.</td>

The Austrasian&nbsp;<a title="Mayor of the Palace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_the_Palace">mayor of the palace</a>&nbsp;<a title="Warnachar II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warnachar_II">Warnachar II</a>&nbsp;recognized him as regent and ordered the army not to resist.</td>

The latter annexed&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasia</a>.</td>

<td>614</td>
<td>18 October</td>
<td><a title="Chlothar II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_II">Chlothar the Great</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<a title="Edict of Paris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_Paris">Edict of Paris</a>. Among its provisions, the edict banned&nbsp;<a title="Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews">Jews</a>&nbsp;from holding royal office and granted the nobility the exclusive power to appoint royal officers.</td>

<td>650</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Synod of Rouen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod_of_Rouen">Synod of Rouen</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholicism">Catholic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;was held in&nbsp;<a title="Rouen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rouen">Rouen</a>&nbsp;which again condemned&nbsp;<a title="Simony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simony">simony</a>.</td>

<td>656</td>
<td>1 February</td>
<td><a title="Sigebert III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigebert_III">Sigebert III</a>&nbsp;died.&nbsp;<a title="Grimoald the Elder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grimoald_the_Elder">Grimoald the Elder</a>&nbsp;tonsured Sigebert's son&nbsp;<a title="Dagobert II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dagobert_II">Dagobert II</a>&nbsp;and declared his own son&nbsp;<a title="Childebert the Adopted" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childebert_the_Adopted">Childebert the Adopted</a>, whom Sigebert III had adopted while still childless,&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasia</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>657</td>
<td>27 November</td>
<td><a title="Clovis II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clovis_II">Clovis II</a>&nbsp;died. His kingdom passed to his young son&nbsp;<a title="Chlothar III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlothar_III">Chlothar III</a>, under the regency of his wife&nbsp;<a title="Balthild" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balthild">Balthild</a>.</td>

<td>661</td>

His younger brother&nbsp;<a title="Theuderic III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theuderic_III">Theuderic III</a>&nbsp;inherited his kingdom with the support of his&nbsp;<a title="Mayor of the Palace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_the_Palace">mayor of the palace</a>&nbsp;<a title="Ebroin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebroin">Ebroin</a>.</td>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">687</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Tertry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Tertry">Battle of Tertry</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasian</a>&nbsp;forces loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Pepin of Herstal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_of_Herstal">Pepin of Herstal</a>&nbsp;defeated the invading army of&nbsp;<a title="Theuderic III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theuderic_III">Theuderic III</a>&nbsp;at modern&nbsp;<a title="Tertry, Somme" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tertry,_Somme">Tertry, Somme</a>. Pepin of Herstal accepted Theuderic's unification of the&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;kingdoms on the condition that he replace&nbsp;<a title="Berthar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berthar">Berthar</a>&nbsp;as his&nbsp;<a title="Mayor of the Palace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_the_Palace">mayor of the palace</a>.</td>

<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of N&icirc;mes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_N%C3%AEmes">Battle of N&icirc;mes</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Charles Martel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Martel">Charles</a>&nbsp;destroyed the&nbsp;<a title="Umayyad Caliphate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate">Umayyad</a>&nbsp;<a title="Septimania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Septimania">Septimanian</a>&nbsp;cities of&nbsp;<a title="N&icirc;mes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N%C3%AEmes">N&icirc;mes</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Agde" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agde">Agde</a>,&nbsp;<a title="B&eacute;ziers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A9ziers">B&eacute;ziers</a>&nbsp;and what is now&nbsp;<a title="Villeneuve-l&egrave;s-Maguelone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Villeneuve-l%C3%A8s-Maguelone">Villeneuve-l&egrave;s-Maguelone</a>.</td>

<td><em><a title="Concilium Germanicum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concilium_Germanicum">Concilium Germanicum</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;called by&nbsp;<a title="Carloman (mayor of the palace)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carloman_(mayor_of_the_palace)">Carloman</a>&nbsp;and presided over by&nbsp;<a title="Saint Boniface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Boniface">Saint Boniface</a>&nbsp;settled some issues of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholicism">Catholic</a>&nbsp;ritual and organization. <td>768</td>
<td>24 September</td>
<td><a title="Pepin the Short" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_the_Short">Pepin the Short</a>&nbsp;died. His kingdom was divided between his sons&nbsp;<a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Carloman I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carloman_I">Carloman I</a>, with the latter receiving territories including the&nbsp;<a title="Paris Basin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Basin">Paris Basin</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Massif Central" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massif_Central">Massif Central</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Provence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provence">Provence</a>, southern&nbsp;<a title="Austrasia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrasia">Austrasia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Alsace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alsace">Alsace</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>25 December</td>
<td><a title="Pope Leo III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Leo_III">Leo</a>&nbsp;crowned&nbsp;<a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h2><span id="9th_century" class="mw-headline">9th century</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Date</th>
<th>Event</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>802</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<em><a title="Capitularia missorum specialia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitularia_missorum_specialia">Capitularia missorum specialia</a></em>, defining the office of the&nbsp;<em><a title="Missus dominicus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missus_dominicus">missus dominicus</a></em>, a salaried emissary to the kingdom.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>803</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<em><a title="Lex Saxonum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lex_Saxonum">Lex Saxonum</a></em>, allowing&nbsp;<a title="Saxons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saxons">Saxon</a>&nbsp;customs which were not contradictory to&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christianity</a>&nbsp;and granting some rights and protections to the church in the Saxon lands.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>804</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;organized the&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Saxony">Duchy of Saxony</a>&nbsp;on the territories of the conquered&nbsp;<a title="Saxons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saxons">Saxons</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>810</td>
<td>8 July</td>
<td><a title="Pepin of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_of_Italy">Pepin of Italy</a>&nbsp;died. He was succeeded as&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>&nbsp;by his illegitimate son&nbsp;<a title="Bernard of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_of_Italy">Bernard of Italy</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>811</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Hemming of Denmark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemming_of_Denmark">Hemming of Denmark</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Denmark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark">Denmark</a>, signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Heiligen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Heiligen">Treaty of Heiligen</a>, promising peace and fixing their border at the&nbsp;<a title="Eider (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eider_(river)">Eider</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>812</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;established the&nbsp;<a title="March of Tuscany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_of_Tuscany">March of Tuscany</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>813</td>
<td>13 September</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;crowned his son&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious, the Fair, the Debonaire</a>&nbsp;co-<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>814</td>
<td>28 January</td>
<td><a title="Charlemagne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>&nbsp;died.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">816</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Pancorbo (816)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Pancorbo_(816)">Battle of Pancorbo (816)</a></em>: Forces loyal to the&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;vassal&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Velasco the Gascon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Velasco_the_Gascon">Velasco the Gascon</a>&nbsp;were routed by the&nbsp;<a title="Emirate of C&oacute;rdoba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba">Emirate of C&oacute;rdoba</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Pancorbo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pancorbo">Pancorbo</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>August</td>
<td><em><a title="Synods of Aachen (816&ndash;819)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synods_of_Aachen_(816%E2%80%93819)">Synods of Aachen (816&ndash;819)</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;was called at the&nbsp;<a title="Palace of Aachen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palace_of_Aachen">Palace of Aachen</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Aachen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aachen">Aachen</a>&nbsp;which would conform&nbsp;<a title="Monk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monk">monks</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Rule of Saint Benedict" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_Saint_Benedict">Rule of Saint Benedict</a>&nbsp;and separate them from&nbsp;<a title="Canon (priest)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canon_(priest)">canons</a>, who were called to live according to the&nbsp;<em><a title="Institutio canonicorum Aquisgranensis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institutio_canonicorum_Aquisgranensis">Institutio canonicorum Aquisgranensis</a></em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>817</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;appointed his son&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a>, his son&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;king of&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, and his son&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;co-<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;with the promise of receiving his other domains.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>818</td>
<td>17 April</td>
<td><a title="Bernard of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_of_Italy">Bernard</a>&nbsp;died, two days after being blinded with a hot poker on&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious's</a>&nbsp;orders.&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;inherited&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>819</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<em><a title="Notitia de servitio monasteriorum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Notitia_de_servitio_monasteriorum">Notitia de servitio monasteriorum</a></em>, which listed monasteries in his kingdom and the services they owed the crown.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>823</td>
<td>5 April</td>
<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;was crowned&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>&nbsp;by the&nbsp;<a title="Pope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope">pope</a>&nbsp;<a title="Pope Paschal I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Paschal_I">Pope Paschal I</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>824</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Roncevaux Pass (824)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Roncevaux_Pass_(824)">Battle of Roncevaux Pass (824)</a></em>: A combined&nbsp;<a title="Basques" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basques">Basque</a>-<a title="Banu Qasi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Qasi">Banu Qasi</a>&nbsp;force defeated a&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;pacifying expedition at&nbsp;<a title="Roncevaux Pass" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roncevaux_Pass">Roncevaux Pass</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>829</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;promised the inheritance of&nbsp;<a title="Alamannia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alamannia">Alamannia</a>&nbsp;to his son&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">830</td>
<td>May</td>
<td>A rebellion of&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>, instigated in part by&nbsp;<a title="Wala of Corbie" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wala_of_Corbie">Wala of Corbie</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Abbot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbot">abbot</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Corbie Abbey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corbie_Abbey">Corbie Abbey</a>, captured their father&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Compi&egrave;gne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compi%C3%A8gne">Compi&egrave;gne</a>&nbsp;and forced their stepmother,&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald's</a>&nbsp;mother&nbsp;<a title="Judith of Bavaria (died 843)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judith_of_Bavaria_(died_843)">Judith of Bavaria (died 843)</a>, into a nunnery.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;declared their loyalty to their father&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;against&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;in exchange for the promise of a greater portion of his inheritance.&nbsp;<a title="Wala of Corbie" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wala_of_Corbie">Wala</a>&nbsp;was deposed as&nbsp;<a title="Abbot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbot">abbot</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Corbie Abbey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corbie_Abbey">Corbie Abbey</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Judith of Bavaria (died 843)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judith_of_Bavaria_(died_843)">Judith</a>&nbsp;returned to her husband's court.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>832</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;declared&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;and promised&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;the rest of his kingdom in the face of an uprising by&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3" valign="top">833</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;joined the rebellion of his brothers&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;against his father&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;met his sons&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;and their armies, as well as the&nbsp;<a title="Pope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope">pope</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pope Gregory IV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Gregory_IV">Pope Gregory IV</a>, at the&nbsp;<a title="Field of Lies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_of_Lies">Field of Lies</a>&nbsp;near&nbsp;<a title="Colmar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colmar">Colmar</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>13 November</td>
<td><a title="Ebbo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebbo">Ebbo</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Archbishop" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archbishop">archbishop</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archdiocese">archdiocese</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Reims" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Reims">Reims</a>, presided over a&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Soissons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soissons">Soissons</a>&nbsp;which deposed&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>834</td>
<td>1 April</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;was restored as&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;with the support of the&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Frankish</a>&nbsp;nobility.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>835</td>
<td>2 February</td>
<td><em><a title="Synod of Thionville" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod_of_Thionville">Synod of Thionville</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Ebbo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebbo">Ebbo</a>&nbsp;publicly recanted his charges against&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;at a&nbsp;<a title="Synod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod">synod</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Thionville" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thionville">Thionville</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>836</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;appointed&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;only of&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>; all else was divided between&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>837</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;crowned&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Alamannia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alamannia">Alamannia</a>&nbsp;and Burgundy, granting him some lands which were before promised to&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>. Louis the German rose in revolt; Louis the Pious responded by promising all his lands save&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria">Bavaria</a>&nbsp;to Charles the Bald.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>838</td>
<td>13 December</td>
<td><a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine</a>&nbsp;died.&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;appointed&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>839</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine">Aquitainian</a>&nbsp;nobility rebelled in favor of&nbsp;<a title="Pepin I of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_I_of_Aquitaine">Pepin I of Aquitaine's</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Pepin II of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_II_of_Aquitaine">Pepin II the Younger of Aquitaine</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;invaded&nbsp;<a title="Swabia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swabia">Swabia</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="5" valign="top">840</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;agreed to a division of the empire after the former's death, with&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;inheriting the western part and Lothair I inheriting the eastern, including&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>Defeated by the forces of&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine">Aquitainian</a>&nbsp;nobility accepted&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of Aquitaine.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;defeated the armies of&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>23 February</td>
<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Pietro Tradonico" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pietro_Tradonico">Pietro Tradonico</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Doge of Venice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doge_of_Venice">doge</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Republic of Venice" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Venice">Republic of Venice</a>, signed the&nbsp;<a title="Pactum Lotharii" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pactum_Lotharii">Pactum Lotharii</a>, reiterating earlier agreements between the&nbsp;<a title="Franks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franks">Franks</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>20 June</td>
<td><a title="Louis the Pious" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Pious">Louis the Pious</a>&nbsp;died.&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;claimed the whole inheritance of his territories as&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">841</td>
<td>25 June</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Fontenoy (841)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Fontenoy_(841)">Battle of Fontenoy</a></em>: The forces of&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;dealt a decisive defeat to&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Pepin II of Aquitaine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepin_II_of_Aquitaine">Pepin the Younger</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Fontenoy, Yonne" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fontenoy,_Yonne">Fontenoy</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>An uprising began among&nbsp;<a title="Saxons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saxons">Saxon</a>&nbsp;peasants who called themselves the&nbsp;<em><a title="Stellinga" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellinga">Stellinga</a></em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>842</td>
<td>12 February</td>
<td><a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;took the&nbsp;<a title="Oaths of Strasbourg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oaths_of_Strasbourg">Oaths of Strasbourg</a>, in which each pledged to aid the other against&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>. Their soldiers pledged not to obey an order counter to this oath.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>843</td>
<td>August</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Verdun" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a>&nbsp;was signed, ending the war between&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>, who received&nbsp;<a title="West Francia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Francia">West Francia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Middle Francia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Francia">Middle Francia</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="East Francia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Francia">East Francia</a>, respectively.&nbsp;<a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;retained the title&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>844</td>
<td>15 June</td>
<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I's</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Louis II of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_II_of_Italy">Louis II of Italy</a>&nbsp;was crowned&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;jointly with his father in&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>&nbsp;by the&nbsp;<a title="Pope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope">pope</a>&nbsp;<a title="Pope Sergius II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Sergius_II">Pope Sergius II</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">855</td>
<td>19 September</td>
<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;and his sons signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Pr&uuml;m" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Pr%C3%BCm">Treaty of Pr&uuml;m</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Sch&uuml;ller" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sch%C3%BCller">Sch&uuml;ller</a>. On his death&nbsp;<a title="Louis II of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_II_of_Italy">Louis II of Italy</a>&nbsp;was to become&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Lothair II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_II">Lothair II</a>&nbsp;king of&nbsp;<a title="Lotharingia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Charles of Provence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_of_Provence">Charles of Provence</a>&nbsp;king of the rest of his domains.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="Lothair I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_I">Lothair I</a>&nbsp;died.</td>

<td>869</td>
<td>8 August</td>
<td><a title="Lothair II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothair_II">Lothair II</a>&nbsp;died.&nbsp;<a title="Lotharingia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>&nbsp;passed to his brother&nbsp;<a title="Louis II of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_II_of_Italy">Louis II</a>, at that time away at war with the&nbsp;<a title="Emirate of Bari" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Bari">Emirate of Bari</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>870</td>
<td>8 August</td>
<td><a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Bald" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Bald">Charles the Bald</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Meersen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Meersen">Treaty of Meersen</a>, under which they agreed to partition&nbsp;<a title="Lotharingia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>&nbsp;between themselves.</td>

<td rowspan="3" valign="top">875</td>

He left&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Italy</a>&nbsp;and the title of&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;to his cousin,&nbsp;<a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German's</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Carloman of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carloman_of_Bavaria">Carloman of Bavaria</a>.</td>

<td rowspan="3" valign="top">876</td>
<td>28 August</td>
<td><a title="Louis the German" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_German">Louis the German</a>&nbsp;died. His kingdom was divided along ethnic lines among his sons&nbsp;<a title="Carloman of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carloman_of_Bavaria">Carloman of Bavaria</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Louis the Younger" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_the_Younger">Louis the Younger</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Fat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Fat">Charles the Fat</a>, who received, roughly,&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria">Bavaria</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Saxony">Saxony</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Swabia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swabia">Swabia</a>, respectively.</td>
</tr>

After converting to&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christianity</a>&nbsp;he was granted the&nbsp;<a title="Kennemerland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kennemerland">Kennemerland</a>&nbsp;as a vassal of&nbsp;<a title="Charles the Fat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_the_Fat">Charles the Fat</a>.</td>

<td>892</td>

<td><a title="Guy III of Spoleto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_III_of_Spoleto">Guy's</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Lambert of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lambert_of_Italy">Lambert of Italy</a>&nbsp;was crowned co-<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;with his father at&nbsp;<a title="Ravenna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ravenna">Ravenna</a>&nbsp;by the&nbsp;<a title="Pope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope">pope</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pope Formosus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Formosus">Pope Formosus</a>.</td>

<td>939</td>
<td>2 October</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Andernach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Andernach">Battle of Andernach</a></em>: A rebellion of&nbsp;<a title="Duchy of Franconia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Franconia">Franconia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lotharingia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>&nbsp;against&nbsp;<a title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Otto the Great</a>&nbsp;was decisively defeated at&nbsp;<a title="Andernach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andernach">Andernach</a>. The&nbsp;<a title="Duke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duke">dukes</a>&nbsp;of Franconia and Lotharingia&nbsp;<a title="Eberhard of Franconia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eberhard_of_Franconia">Eberhard of Franconia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Gilbert, Duke of Lorraine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilbert,_Duke_of_Lorraine">Gilbert</a>&nbsp;were killed. Otto the Great prevented succession in both duchies and dissolved the former.</td>

<td>962</td>
<td>2 February</td>
<td><a title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Otto the Great</a>&nbsp;was crowned&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>965</td>
<td>20 May</td>
<td><a title="Gero" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gero">Gero</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Margrave" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margrave">margrave</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<em><a title="Marca Geronis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marca_Geronis">Marca Geronis</a></em>, died. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="March (territorial entity)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_(territorial_entity)">march</a>&nbsp;was divided into five: the&nbsp;<a title="Northern March" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_March">Northern March</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Saxon Eastern March" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saxon_Eastern_March">Saxon Eastern March</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Margravate of Meissen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margravate_of_Meissen">Margravate of Meissen</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="March of Zeitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_of_Zeitz">March of Zeitz</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="March of Merseburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_of_Merseburg">March of Merseburg</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>967</td>
<td>25 December</td>
<td><a title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Otto the Great's</a>&nbsp;young son&nbsp;<a title="Otto II, Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor">Otto II the Red, Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;was crowned co-<a title="Holy Roman Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>&nbsp;with his father by the&nbsp;<a title="Pope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope">pope</a>&nbsp;<a title="Pope John XIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_XIII">Pope John XIII</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>972</td>
<td>24 June</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Cedynia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Cedynia">Battle of Cedynia</a></em>: The forces of&nbsp;<a title="Odo I, Margrave of the Saxon Ostmark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odo_I,_Margrave_of_the_Saxon_Ostmark">Odo I, Margrave of the Saxon Ostmark</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Margrave" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margrave">margrave</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Saxon Eastern March" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saxon_Eastern_March">Saxon Eastern March</a>, were decisively repelled by the&nbsp;<a title="Polans (western)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polans_(western)">Polans</a>&nbsp;near the&nbsp;<a title="Oder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oder">Oder</a>, possibly near&nbsp;<a title="Cedynia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedynia">Cedynia</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">973</td>

<td>1414</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Council of Constance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Constance">Council of Constance</a></em>: An&nbsp;<a title="Ecumenical council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecumenical_council">ecumenical council</a>&nbsp;began which would condemn&nbsp;<a title="Jan Hus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Hus">Jan Hus</a>&nbsp;as a&nbsp;<a title="Heresy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy">heretic</a>, depose&nbsp;<a title="Antipope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipope">Antipopes</a>&nbsp;<a title="Antipope John XXIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipope_John_XXIII">John XXIII</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Antipope Benedict XIII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipope_Benedict_XIII">Benedict XIII</a>, and elect&nbsp;<a title="Pope Martin V" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Martin_V">Pope Martin V</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1418</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Council of Constance</em>: The council ended.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1455</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Gutenberg Bible" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible">Gutenberg Bible</a>, one of the first books in the West made using moveable type, was first printed by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Johann Gutenberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Gutenberg">Johann Gutenberg</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>1495</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)">Imperial Diet</a>&nbsp;established the&nbsp;<em><a title="Reichskammergericht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichskammergericht">Reichskammergericht</a></em>, a permanent court of appeal with jurisdiction over the whole of the&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.</td>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1745</td>
<td>4 June</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Hohenfriedberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenfriedberg">Battle of Hohenfriedberg</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussian</a>&nbsp;force led by&nbsp;<a title="Frederick the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_the_Great">Frederick the Great</a>&nbsp;decisively defeated the allied armies of&nbsp;<a title="Archduchy of Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria">Austria</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Electorate of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony">Saxony</a>, halting the attempted reconquest of&nbsp;<a title="Silesia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silesia">Silesia</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>25 December</td>
<td><em>Silesian Wars</em>:&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Archduchy of Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria">Austria</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Electorate of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony">Saxony</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Dresden" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Dresden">Treaty of Dresden</a>, confirming Prussia's sovereignty over&nbsp;<a title="Silesia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silesia">Silesia</a>&nbsp;and ending the war.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1750</td>
<td>28 July</td>
<td><a title="Johann Sebastian Bach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach">Bach</a>&nbsp;died.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>29 August</td>
<td><em><a title="Third Silesian War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Silesian_War">Third Silesian War</a></em>&nbsp;(<em><a title="Seven Years' War" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War">Seven Years' War</a></em>):&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussia</a>&nbsp;invaded&nbsp;<a title="Electorate of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony">Saxony</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1763</td>
<td>15 February</td>
<td><em>Third Silesian War</em>:&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Archduchy of Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria">Austria</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Electorate of Saxony" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony">Saxony</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Hubertusburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a>, ending the war and restoring the three states' prewar borders.</td>
</tr>

<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1791</td>
<td>27 August</td>
<td><a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussia</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Holy Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<a title="Declaration of Pillnitz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_Pillnitz">Declaration of Pillnitz</a>, promising to join a coalition to restore&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XVI of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France">Louis XVI of France</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_France">French</a>&nbsp;throne.</td>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1792</td>

<td><em><a title="French Revolutionary Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a></em>:&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of France (1791&ndash;92)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_France_(1791%E2%80%9392)">France</a>&nbsp;declared war on&nbsp;<a title="Archduchy of Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria">Austria</a>.</td>

<td>25 July</td>

<td>20 May</td>

<td>1849</td>
<td>18 June</td>
<td><em>German revolutions of 1848&ndash;49</em>: The chamber of the&nbsp;<a title="Frankfurt Parliament" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankfurt_Parliament">Frankfurt Parliament</a>, since reduced to a rump parliament and moved to&nbsp;<a title="Stuttgart" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, was occupied by the&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of W&uuml;rttemberg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg">W&uuml;rttemberg</a>&nbsp;army. <td rowspan="2" valign="top">1850</td>
<td>30 May</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Prussian three-class franchise" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_three-class_franchise">Prussian three-class franchise</a>, according to which all males over the age of 24 were allowed to vote for their representatives in the lower house of the&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussian</a>&nbsp;parliament, with votes weighted by amount of taxes paid, was introduced.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>29 November</td>
<td><a title="Kingdom of Prussia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">Prussia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Austrian Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Empire">Austria</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Punctuation of Olm&uuml;tz" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punctuation_of_Olm%C3%BCtz">Punctuation of Olm&uuml;tz</a>, under which the former agreed to the dissolution of the Prussian-led&nbsp;<a title="Erfurt Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erfurt_Union">Erfurt Union</a>&nbsp;and the revival of the&nbsp;<a title="German Confederation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Confederation">German Confederation</a>&nbsp;under Austrian leadership.</td>

<td><em><a title="Berlin Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Conference">Berlin Conference</a></em>: A conference was convened in&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>&nbsp;to formalize the practice of territorial claims in&nbsp;<a title="Africa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa">Africa</a>&nbsp;by the participating powers&nbsp;<a title="Austria-Hungary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Belgium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium">Belgium</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Denmark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark">Denmark</a>,&nbsp;<a title="French Third Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic">France</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland">United Kingdom</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Italy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy">Italy</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Netherlands" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands">Netherlands</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Portugal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal">Portugal</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Restoration (Spain)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restoration_(Spain)">Spain</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Union between Sweden and Norway" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_between_Sweden_and_Norway">Sweden-Norway</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Ottoman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>10 November</td>
<td><em>German Revolution of 1918&ndash;19</em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Council of the People's Deputies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_the_People%27s_Deputies">Council of the People's Deputies</a>, a body elected from the&nbsp;<a title="Workers' council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_council">workers' councils</a>&nbsp;of Berlin, introduced sweeping liberal reforms including the elimination of the&nbsp;<a title="Prussian three-class franchise" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_three-class_franchise">Prussian three-class franchise</a>&nbsp;and women's suffrage.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>11 November</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="5" valign="top">1919</td>
<td>15 January</td>
<td><em><a title="Spartacist uprising" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spartacist_uprising">Spartacist uprising</a></em>: The&nbsp;<em><a title="Freikorps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freikorps">Freikorps</a></em>&nbsp;crushed a Berlin uprising by the&nbsp;<a title="Marxism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism">Marxist</a>&nbsp;<a title="Spartacus League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spartacus_League">Spartacus League</a>, killing some hundred and fifty civilians and executing their leaders&nbsp;<a title="Karl Liebknecht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Liebknecht">Karl Liebknecht</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Rosa Luxemburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg">Rosa Luxemburg</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>11 February</td>

<tr>
<td>6 April</td>
<td><a title="Ernst Toller" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Toller">Ernst Toller</a>&nbsp;declared the establishment of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian Council Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavarian_Council_Republic">Bavarian Council Republic</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavaria">Bavaria</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>28 June</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919">Paris Peace Conference, 1919</a></em>: Representatives of some thirty world powers signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Versailles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, under which Germany was forced to disarm, give up its colonies, make substantial territorial concessions, and pay reparations to the&nbsp;<a title="Allies of World War I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I">Allies</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>11 August</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Weimar Constitution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weimar_Constitution">Weimar Constitution</a>&nbsp;came into force. The Weimar Republic succeeded the German Empire.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1920</td>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">13 March</td>
<td><em><a title="Kapp Putsch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kapp_Putsch">Kapp Putsch</a></em>: The&nbsp;<em><a title="Freikorps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freikorps">Freikorps</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Marinebrigade Ehrhardt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marinebrigade_Ehrhardt">Marinebrigade Ehrhardt</a>&nbsp;occupied&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Wolfgang Kapp" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfgang_Kapp">Wolfgang Kapp</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="National conservatism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_conservatism">national conservative</a>&nbsp;<a title="German National People's Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_National_People%27s_Party">German National People's Party (DNVP)</a>&nbsp;declared himself&nbsp;<a title="Chancellor of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany">chancellor</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><em><a title="Ruhr uprising" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr_uprising">Ruhr uprising</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Communist Party of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Germany">Communist Party of Germany</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Communist Workers' Party of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Workers%27_Party_of_Germany">Communist Workers' Party of Germany</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Independent Social Democratic Party of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany">Independent Social Democratic Party of Germany</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Free Workers' Union of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Workers%27_Union_of_Germany">Free Workers' Union of Germany</a>&nbsp;together established the&nbsp;<a title="Ruhr Red Army" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr_Red_Army">Ruhr Red Army</a>, which expelled the&nbsp;<em><a title="Freikorps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freikorps">Freikorps</a></em>&nbsp;from the valley of the&nbsp;<a title="Ruhr (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr_(river)">Ruhr</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1921</td>
<td>June</td>
<td><em><a title="Hyperinflation in the Weimar Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperinflation_in_the_Weimar_Republic">Hyperinflation in the Weimar Republic</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Inflation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation">Inflation</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="German Papiermark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Papiermark">Papiermark (Mark)</a>&nbsp;began in response to the first reparations payment to the&nbsp;<a title="Allies of World War I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I">Allies</a>&nbsp;under the terms of the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Versailles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1922</td>
<td>16 April</td>
<td>Germany and&nbsp;<a title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic">Russia</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Rapallo (1922)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Rapallo_(1922)">Treaty of Rapallo</a>, in which each renounced all territorial and financial claims against the other and pledged to normalize relations.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3" valign="top">1923</td>
<td>11 January</td>
<td><em><a title="Occupation of the Ruhr" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Ruhr">Occupation of the Ruhr</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="French Third Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic">France</a>&nbsp;invaded the valley of the&nbsp;<a title="Ruhr (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr_(river)">Ruhr</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>13 August</td>
<td><a title="Gustav Stresemann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Stresemann">Gustav Stresemann</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="National liberalism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_liberalism">national liberal</a>&nbsp;<a title="German People's Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_People%27s_Party">German People's Party</a>&nbsp;was appointed&nbsp;<a title="Chancellor of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany">chancellor</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Minister for Foreign Affairs (Germany)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_for_Foreign_Affairs_(Germany)">minister for foreign affairs</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>8 November</td>
<td><em><a title="Beer Hall Putsch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi Party</a>&nbsp;chairman&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>&nbsp;led some six hundred&nbsp;<a title="Sturmabteilung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sturmabteilung"><em>Sturmabteilung</em>&nbsp;(SA)</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="B&uuml;rgerbr&auml;ukeller" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerbr%C3%A4ukeller">B&uuml;rgerbr&auml;ukeller</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Munich" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich">Munich</a>, where they held&nbsp;<a title="Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavaria">Bavarian</a>&nbsp;state officials&nbsp;<a title="Gustav Ritter von Kahr" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Ritter_von_Kahr">Gustav Ritter von Kahr</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Hans Ritter von Seisser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Ritter_von_Seisser">Hans Ritter von Seisser</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Otto von Lossow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_von_Lossow">Otto von Lossow</a>&nbsp;at gunpoint to demand they support a Nazi&nbsp;<em>coup</em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1924</td>
<td>August</td>
<td>Germany and the&nbsp;<a title="Triple Entente" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_Entente">Triple Entente</a>&nbsp;agreed to the&nbsp;<a title="Dawes Plan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dawes_Plan">Dawes Plan</a>&nbsp;negotiated by head of the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;<a title="Office of Management and Budget" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget">Bureau of the Budget</a>&nbsp;chief&nbsp;<a title="Charles G. Dawes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_G._Dawes">Charles G. Dawes</a>, under which the&nbsp;<a title="French Third Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic">French</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Belgium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium">Belgian</a>&nbsp;occupation of the&nbsp;<a title="Ruhr (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr_(river)">Ruhr</a>&nbsp;valley was ended and the reparation payment schedule restructured.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1925</td>
<td>16 October</td>
<td>The last of the&nbsp;<a title="Locarno Treaties" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Locarno_Treaties">Locarno Treaties</a>, under which&nbsp;<a title="French Third Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic">France</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Belgium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium">Belgium</a>&nbsp;and Germany settled their borders and pledged not to attack each other, was signed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1926</td>
<td>8 September</td>
<td>Germany joined the&nbsp;<a title="League of Nations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations">League of Nations</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3" valign="top">1929</td>
<td>31 August</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Allies of World War I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I">Allies</a>&nbsp;accepted the&nbsp;<a title="Young Plan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Plan">Young Plan</a>, which reduced Germany's war reparations and allowed it to defer a greater portion, which would accrue interest due to a consortium of&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">American</a>&nbsp;banks.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3 October</td>
<td><a title="Gustav Stresemann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Stresemann">Stresemann</a>&nbsp;died.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>29 October</td>
<td><em><a title="Wall Street Crash of 1929" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Dow Jones Industrial Average" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>&nbsp;dropped twelve percent in a trading session of record volume.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1930</td>
<td>14 September</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="German federal election, 1930" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_federal_election,_1930">German federal election, 1930</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Social Democratic Party of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany">SPD</a>&nbsp;retained a plurality of seats in the&nbsp;<a title="Reichstag (Weimar Republic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_(Weimar_Republic)">Reichstag</a>. The&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi Party</a>&nbsp;gained ninety-five seats.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="6" valign="top">1933</td>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">30 January</td>
<td><a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Hitler</a>&nbsp;was appointed&nbsp;<a title="Chancellor of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany">chancellor</a>&nbsp;at the head of a&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi</a>-<a title="German National People's Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_National_People%27s_Party">DNVP</a>&nbsp;coalition.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The process of&nbsp;<em><a title="Gleichschaltung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gleichschaltung">Gleichschaltung</a></em>, in which the government dismantled non-<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi</a>&nbsp;parties and societies, began.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>27 February</td>
<td><em><a title="Reichstag fire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_fire">Reichstag fire</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Reichstag building" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_building">Reichstag building</a>&nbsp;was burned. The&nbsp;<a title="Dutch people" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_people">Dutch</a>&nbsp;<a title="Council communism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_communism">council communist</a>&nbsp;<a title="Marinus van der Lubbe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marinus_van_der_Lubbe">Marinus van der Lubbe</a>&nbsp;was caught at the scene and confessed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>28 February</td>
<td><a title="President of Germany (1919&ndash;1945)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Germany_(1919%E2%80%931945)">President</a>&nbsp;<a title="Paul von Hindenburg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_von_Hindenburg">Paul von Hindenburg</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<a title="Reichstag Fire Decree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_Fire_Decree">Reichstag Fire Decree</a>, suspending most civil liberties.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>24 March</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Enabling Act of 1933" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enabling_Act_of_1933">Enabling Act of 1933</a>, which granted the cabinet the power to make laws, was passed and signed in the presence of armed members of the&nbsp;<a title="Sturmabteilung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sturmabteilung">SA</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Schutzstaffel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schutzstaffel"><em>Schutzstaffel</em>&nbsp;(SS)</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>20 July</td>
<td><a title="Vice-Chancellor of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice-Chancellor_of_Germany">Vice-chancellor</a>&nbsp;<a title="Franz von Papen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_von_Papen">Franz von Papen</a>&nbsp;of Germany and&nbsp;<a title="Cardinal Secretary of State" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardinal_Secretary_of_State">cardinal secretary of state</a>&nbsp;<a title="Pope Pius XII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII">Pope Pius XII</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Holy See" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_See">Holy See</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<em><a title="Reichskonkordat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichskonkordat">Reichskonkordat</a></em>, which required&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop (Catholic Church)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bishop_(Catholic_Church)">bishops</a>&nbsp;to swear loyalty to the&nbsp;<a title="President of Germany (1919&ndash;1945)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Germany_(1919%E2%80%931945)">president</a>&nbsp;of Germany.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3" valign="top">1934</td>
<td>30 June</td>
<td><em><a title="Night of the Long Knives" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_of_the_Long_Knives">Night of the Long Knives</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Schutzstaffel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schutzstaffel">SS</a>&nbsp;paramilitaries killed at least eighty-five potential threats to&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Hitler's</a>&nbsp;power, including&nbsp;<a title="Sturmabteilung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sturmabteilung">SA</a>&nbsp;head&nbsp;<a title="Ernst R&ouml;hm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_R%C3%B6hm">Ernst R&ouml;hm</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Gregor Strasser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregor_Strasser">Gregor Strasser</a>, head of the&nbsp;<a title="Left-wing politics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics">left wing</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Nazi Party" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party">Nazi Party</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1 August</td>
<td><a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Hitler</a>&nbsp;issued a law merging the powers of the&nbsp;<a title="President of Germany (1919&ndash;1945)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Germany_(1919%E2%80%931945)">presidency</a>&nbsp;into the office of the&nbsp;<a title="Chancellor of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany">chancellor</a>.</td>

<td>1935</td>
<td>16 March</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="German re-armament" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_re-armament">German re-armament</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Adolf Hitler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler">Hitler</a>&nbsp;announced that Germany would rebuild its military, in violation of the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Versailles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1936</td>
<td>7 March</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Remilitarisation of the Rhineland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remilitarisation_of_the_Rhineland">Remilitarisation of the Rhineland</a></em>: German troops entered the&nbsp;<a title="Rhineland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhineland">Rhineland</a>&nbsp;in violation of the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Versailles" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="1936 Summer Olympics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a></em>: Germany won the greatest number of gold, silver and bronze medals at the Olympics, held in&nbsp;<a title="Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a>.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="African American" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_American">Black</a>&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">American</a>&nbsp;<a title="Jesse Owens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Owens">Jesse Owens</a>&nbsp;won four gold medals, the highest individual total.</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>9 November</td>
<td><em><a title="Kristallnacht" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Pogrom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom">pogrom</a>&nbsp;took place in which&nbsp;<a title="Sturmabteilung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sturmabteilung">SA</a>&nbsp;paramilitaries and German civilians destroyed&nbsp;<a title="Jews" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews">Jewish</a>&nbsp;businesses and at least ninety-one were killed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1939</td>
<td>23 August</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Molotov&ndash;Ribbentrop Pact" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact">Molotov&ndash;Ribbentrop Pact</a>&nbsp;was signed, promising mutual non-aggression between Germany and the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>&nbsp;and agreeing to a division of much of&nbsp;<a title="Eastern Europe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe">Eastern Europe</a>&nbsp;between those two countries.</td>

</tr>
