<tr>
<td>1 August</td>
<td><em><a title="Potsdam Conference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potsdam_Conference">Potsdam Conference</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">British</a>&nbsp;<a title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom">prime minister</a>&nbsp;<a title="Clement Attlee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clement_Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>,&nbsp;<a title="President of the United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States">president</a>&nbsp;<a title="Harry S. Truman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_S._Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Joseph Stalin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union">general secretary</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet</a>&nbsp;<a title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union">Communist Party</a>, issued the&nbsp;<a title="Potsdam Agreement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potsdam_Agreement">Potsdam Agreement</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Cecilienhof" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cecilienhof">Cecilienhof</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Potsdam" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potsdam">Potsdam</a>. The parties agreed that Germany would be returned to its 1937 borders with some additional cessions to the Soviet Union and ratified its division into British,&nbsp;<a title="Provisional Government of the French Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_French_Republic">French</a>, American and Soviet occupation zones.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1946</td>
<td>29 March</td>
<td>The first of the&nbsp;<a title="Allied plans for German industry after World War II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_plans_for_German_industry_after_World_War_II">Allied plans for German industry after World War II</a>, which called for the reduction of German industrial capacity, was issued by the&nbsp;<a title="Allied Control Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_Control_Council">Allied Control Council</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6 September</td>
<td><a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;<a title="United States Secretary of State" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State">secretary of state</a>&nbsp;<a title="James F. Byrnes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_F._Byrnes">James F. Byrnes</a>&nbsp;read the speech&nbsp;<a title="Restatement of Policy on Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restatement_of_Policy_on_Germany">Restatement of Policy on Germany</a>, clarifying his nation's desire for economic recovery in Germany and guaranteeing its borders.</td>

<td rowspan="4" valign="top">1948</td>
<td>20 June</td>
<td><a title="Ludwig Erhard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludwig_Erhard">Ludwig Erhard</a>, the appointed economic director of the&nbsp;<a title="Bizone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bizone">Bizone</a>, introduced the&nbsp;<a title="Deutsche Mark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Mark">Deutsche Mark</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>24 June</td>
<td><em><a title="Berlin Blockade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>&nbsp;blocked&nbsp;<a title="Western Bloc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Bloc">Western Bloc</a>&nbsp;access to&nbsp;<a title="West Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Berlin">West Berlin</a>&nbsp;by road and rail.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>25 June</td>
<td><em>Berlin Blockade</em>:&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;cargo planes began shipping food and medical supplies to&nbsp;<a title="West Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Berlin">West Berlin</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>12 December</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)">Free Democratic Party (FDP)</a>&nbsp;was established.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="5" valign="top">1949</td>
<td>12 May</td>
<td><em>Berlin Blockade</em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>&nbsp;lifted the blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_E._Griffin_1948_20-0" class="reference"></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>23 May</td>
<td><a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>&nbsp;was founded.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>14 August</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="West German federal election, 1949" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_German_federal_election,_1949">West German federal election, 1949</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Christian Democratic Union of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany">CDU</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Christian Social Union in Bavaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Social_Union_in_Bavaria">Christian Social Union in Bavaria (CSU)</a>&nbsp;won a narrow plurality of seats in the&nbsp;<a title="Bundestag" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bundestag">Bundestag</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>15 September</td>
<td><a title="Konrad Adenauer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Christian Democratic Union of Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany">CDU</a>&nbsp;became&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (1949&ndash;)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(1949%E2%80%93)">chancellor</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>.</td>

<td>1950</td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Wirtschaftswunder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder">Wirtschaftswunder</a></em>:&nbsp;<em><a title="The Times" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times">The Times</a></em>&nbsp;first used the term&nbsp;<em>Wirtschaftswunder</em>&nbsp;to refer to the rapid postwar economic growth of&nbsp;<a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Austria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria">Austria</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1951</td>
<td>18 April</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Inner Six" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_Six">Inner Six</a>&nbsp;<a title="Europe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe">European</a>&nbsp;nations including&nbsp;<a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>&nbsp;signed the&nbsp;<a title="Treaty of Paris (1951)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)">Treaty of Paris</a>&nbsp;establishing the&nbsp;<a title="European Coal and Steel Community" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Single market" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_market">single market</a>&nbsp;in coal and steel governed by supranational institutions.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1952</td>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">26 May</td>
<td><a title="East Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany">East Germany</a>&nbsp;strengthened its border protection regime along the&nbsp;<a title="Inner German border" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_German_border">Inner German border</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="General Treaty" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Treaty">General Treaty</a>, which granted&nbsp;<a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>&nbsp;the "authority of a&nbsp;<a title="Sovereign state" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereign_state">sovereign state</a>", was signed by West Germany,&nbsp;<a title="French Fourth Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic">France</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">1953</td>
<td>16 June</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Uprising of 1953 in East Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uprising_of_1953_in_East_Germany">Uprising of 1953 in East Germany</a></em>: In response to a 10 percent increase in work quotas, between 60 and 80 construction workers went on strike in&nbsp;<a title="East Berlin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Berlin">East Berlin</a>. Their numbers quickly swelled and a general strike and protests were called for the next day.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>17 June</td>
<td><em>Uprising of 1953 in East Germany</em>: 100,000 protestors gathered at dawn, demanding the reinstatement of old work quotas and, later, the resignation of the&nbsp;<a title="East Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany">East German</a>&nbsp;government. At noon German police trapped many of the demonstrators in an open square;&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet</a>&nbsp;tanks fired on the crowd, killing hundreds and ending the protest.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1954</td>
<td>4 July</td>
<td><em><a title="1954 FIFA World Cup Final" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup_Final">1954 FIFA World Cup Final</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="West Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany">West Germany</a>&nbsp;defeated the heavily favored&nbsp;<a title="Hungarian People's Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic">Hungarian</a>&nbsp;national team in the final match of the&nbsp;<a title="FIFA World Cup" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Bern" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bern">Bern</a>.</td>

<td><a title="People's Socialist Republic of Albania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania">Albania</a>,&nbsp;<a title="People's Republic of Bulgaria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic">Czechoslovakia</a>,&nbsp;<a title="East Germany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany">East Germany</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Hungarian People's Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic">Hungary</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Polish People's Republic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic">Poland</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Socialist Republic of Romania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania">Romania</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Soviet Union" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</a>&nbsp;established the&nbsp;<a title="Warsaw Pact" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, a collective defense organization.</td>

<td>1968</td>

<td>12 August</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>7 December</td>
